# OWASP ZAP Scan Report

## Target Information
- **Target**: http://192.168.1.49:3000
- **ZAP Version**: 2.17.0
- **Mode**: daemon
- **Spider**: True
- **AJAX Spider**: True
- **Active Scan**: True
- **Total Alerts**: 1041

## Scan Timing

**Total Duration**: 4m 12s

### Phase Breakdown

- **ZAP Connection & Verification**: 0.0s
- **Seed URL Access**: 0.3s
- **Spider Scan**: 16.0s
- **AJAX Spider Scan**: 0.0s
- **Active Scan**: 3m 55s
- **Passive Scan Queue Drain**: 0.0s
- **Alert Collection**: 0.2s

## Warnings

- Failed to disable robots.txt handling: Failed to parse JSON from http://127.0.0.1:8080/JSON/spider/action/setOptionHandleRobotsTxt/?apikey=&Boolean=false: HTTP Error 400: Bad Request
- AJAX spider failed: Failed to parse JSON from http://127.0.0.1:8080/JSON/spiderAjax/action/scan/?apikey=&url=http%3A%2F%2F192.168.1.49%3A3000: HTTP Error 400: Bad Request

## Alerts

### 1. Content Security Policy (CSP) Header Not Set

**Risk**: MEDIUM | **Confidence**: High

**URL**: `http://192.168.1.49:3000`

**Description**: Content Security Policy (CSP) is an added layer of security that helps to detect and mitigate certain types of attacks, including Cross Site Scripting (XSS) and data injection attacks. These attacks are used for everything from data theft to site defacement or distribution of malware. CSP provides a set of standard HTTP headers that allow website owners to declare approved sources of content that browsers should be allowed to load on that page — covered types are JavaScript, CSS, HTML frames, fonts, images and embeddable objects such as Java applets, ActiveX, audio and video files.

**Solution**: Ensure that your web server, application server, load balancer, etc. is configured to set the Content-Security-Policy header.

---

---

### 4. Cross-Domain Misconfiguration

**Risk**: MEDIUM | **Confidence**: Medium

**URL**: `http://192.168.1.49:3000/api/Addresss/:id`

**Evidence**: `Access-Control-Allow-Origin: *`

**Description**: Web browser data loading may be possible, due to a Cross Origin Resource Sharing (CORS) misconfiguration on the web server.

**Solution**: Ensure that sensitive data is not available in an unauthenticated manner (using IP address white-listing, for instance).
Configure the "Access-Control-Allow-Origin" HTTP header to a more restrictive set of domains, or remove all CORS headers entirely, to allow the web browser to enforce the Same Origin Policy (SOP) in a more restrictive manner.

---

### 18. Application Error Disclosure

**Risk**: LOW | **Confidence**: Medium

**URL**: `http://192.168.1.49:3000/api/Hints`

**Evidence**: `HTTP/1.1 500 Internal Server Error`

**Description**: This page contains an error/warning message that may disclose sensitive information like the location of the file that produced the unhandled exception. This information can be used to launch further attacks against the web application. The alert could be a false positive if the error message is found inside a documentation page.

**Solution**: Review the source code of this page. Implement custom error pages. Consider implementing a mechanism to provide a unique error reference/identifier to the client (browser) while logging the details on the server side and not exposing them to the user.

---

**Description**: This page contains an error/warning message that may disclose sensitive information like the location of the file that produced the unhandled exception. **Description**: Content Security Policy (CSP) is an added layer of security that helps to detect and mitigate certain types of attacks, including Cross Site Scripting (XSS) and data injection attacks. These attacks are used for everything from data theft to site defacement or distribution of malware. CSP provides a set of standard HTTP headers that allow website owners to declare approved sources of content that browsers should be allowed to load on that page — covered types are JavaScript, CSS, HTML frames, fonts, images and embeddable objects such as Java applets, ActiveX, audio and video files.

**Solution**: Ensure that your web server, application server, load balancer, etc. is configured to set the Content-Security-Policy header.

---

### 43. Cross-Domain Misconfiguration

**Risk**: MEDIUM | **Confidence**: Medium

**URL**: `http://192.168.1.49:3000/redirect`

**Evidence**: `Access-Control-Allow-Origin: *`

**Description**: Web browser data loading may be possible, due to a Cross Origin Resource Sharing (CORS) misconfiguration on the web server.

**Solution**: Ensure that sensitive data is not available in an unauthenticated manner (using IP address white-listing, for instance).
Configure the "Access-Control-Allow-Origin" HTTP header to a more restrictive set of domains, or remove all CORS headers entirely, to allow the web browser to enforce the Same Origin Policy (SOP) in a more restrictive manner.

---

### 50. Private IP Disclosure

**Risk**: LOW | **Confidence**: Medium

**URL**: `http://192.168.1.49:3000/profile`

**Evidence**: `192.168.1.144`

**Description**: A private IP (such as 10.x.x.x, 172.x.x.x, 192.168.x.x) or an Amazon EC2 private hostname (for example, ip-10-0-56-78) has been found in the HTTP response body. This information might be helpful for further attacks targeting internal systems.

**Solution**: Remove the private IP address from the HTTP response body. For comments, use JSP/ASP/PHP comment instead of HTML/JavaScript comment which can be seen by client browsers.

---

### 51. Application Error Disclosure

**Risk**: LOW | **Confidence**: Medium

**URL**: `http://192.168.1.49:3000/rest/2fa/verify`

**Evidence**: `HTTP/1.1 500 Internal Server Error`

**Description**: This page contains an error/warning message that may disclose sensitive information like the location of the file that produced the unhandled exception. This information can be used to launch further attacks against the web application. The alert could be a false positive if the error message is found inside a documentation page.

**Solution**: Review the source code of this page. Implement custom error pages. Consider implementing a mechanism to provide a unique error reference/identifier to the client (browser) while logging the details on the server side and not exposing them to the user.

### 69. X-Content-Type-Options Header Missing

**Risk**: LOW | **Confidence**: Medium

**URL**: `http://192.168.1.49:3000/metrics`

**Description**: The Anti-MIME-Sniffing header X-Content-Type-Options was not set to 'nosniff'. This allows older versions of Internet Explorer and Chrome to perform MIME-sniffing on the response body, potentially causing the response body to be interpreted and displayed as a content type other than the declared content type. Current (early 2014) and legacy versions of Firefox will use the declared content type (if one is set), rather than performing MIME-sniffing.

**Solution**: Ensure that the application/web server sets the Content-Type header appropriately, and that it sets the X-Content-Type-Options header to 'nosniff' for all web pages.
If possible, ensure that the end user uses a standards-compliant and modern web browser that does not perform MIME-sniffing at all, or that can be directed by the web application/web server to not perform MIME-sniffing.

---

**Evidence**: `192.168.99.100:3000`

**Description**: A private IP (such as 10.x.x.x, 172.x.x.x, 192.168.x.x) or an Amazon EC2 private hostname (for example, ip-10-0-56-78) has been found in the HTTP response body. This information might be helpful for further attacks targeting internal systems.

**Solution**: Remove the private IP address from the HTTP response body. For comments, use JSP/ASP/PHP comment instead of HTML/JavaScript comment which can be seen by client browsers.

---

### 85. Application Error Disclosure

**Risk**: LOW | **Confidence**: Medium

**URL**: `http://192.168.1.49:3000/rest/order-history`

**Evidence**: `HTTP/1.1 500 Internal Server Error`

**Description**: This page contains an error/warning message that may disclose sensitive information like the location of the file that produced the unhandled exception. This information can be used to launch further attacks against the web application. The alert could be a false positive if the error message is found inside a documentation page.

**Solution**: Review the source code of this page. Implement custom error pages. Consider implementing a mechanism to provide a unique error reference/identifier to the client (browser) while logging the details on the server side and not exposing them to the user.

---

### 86. Application Error Disclosure

**Risk**: LOW | **Confidence**: Medium

**URL**: `http://192.168.1.49:3000/rest/order-history/:id/delivery-status`

**Evidence**: `HTTP/1.1 500 Internal Server Error`

**Description**: This page contains an error/warning message that may disclose sensitive information like the location of the file that produced the unhandled exception. This information can be used to launch further attacks against the web application. The alert could be a false positive if the error message is found inside a documentation page.

**Solution**: Review the source code of this page. Implement custom error pages. Consider implementing a mechanism to provide a unique error reference/identifier to the client (browser) while logging the details on the server side and not exposing them to the user.

---

### 87. Content Security Policy (CSP) Header Not Set

**Risk**: MEDIUM | **Confidence**: High

**URL**: `http://192.168.1.49:3000/rest/order-history/:id/delivery-status`

**Description**: Content Security Policy (CSP) is an added layer of security that helps to detect and mitigate certain types of attacks, including Cross Site Scripting (XSS) and data injection attacks. These attacks are used for everything from data theft to site defacement or distribution of malware. CSP provides a set of standard HTTP headers that allow website owners to declare approved sources of content that browsers should be allowed to load on that page — covered types are JavaScript, CSS, HTML frames, fonts, images and embeddable objects such as Java applets, ActiveX, audio and video files.

**Solution**: Ensure that your web server, application server, load balancer, etc. is configured to set the Content-Security-Policy header.

---

### 88. Cross-Domain Misconfiguration

**Risk**: MEDIUM | **Confidence**: Medium

**URL**: `http://192.168.1.49:3000/rest/order-history/:id/delivery-status`

**Evidence**: `Access-Control-Allow-Origin: *`

**Description**: Web browser data loading may be possible, due to a Cross Origin Resource Sharing (CORS) misconfiguration on the web server.

**Solution**: Ensure that sensitive data is not available in an unauthenticated manner (using IP address white-listing, for instance).
Configure the "Access-Control-Allow-Origin" HTTP header to a more restrictive set of domains, or remove all CORS headers entirely, to allow the web browser to enforce the Same Origin Policy (SOP) in a more restrictive manner.

---

**Evidence**: `Access-Control-Allow-Origin: *`

**Description**: Web browser data loading may be possible, due to a Cross Origin Resource Sharing (CORS) misconfiguration on the web server.

**Solution**: Ensure that sensitive data is not available in an unauthenticated manner (using IP address white-listing, for instance).
Configure the "Access-Control-Allow-Origin" HTTP header to a more restrictive set of domains, or remove all CORS headers entirely, to allow the web browser to enforce the Same Origin Policy (SOP) in a more restrictive manner.

---

### 129. Cross-Domain JavaScript Source File Inclusion

**Risk**: LOW | **Confidence**: Medium

**URL**: `http://192.168.1.49:3000/b2b`

**Evidence**: `<script src="//cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/jquery/2.2.4/jquery.min.js"></script>`

**Description**: The page includes one or more script files from a third-party domain.

**Solution**: Ensure JavaScript source files are loaded from only trusted sources, and the sources can't be controlled by end users of the application.

### 131. Content Security Policy (CSP) Header Not Set

**Risk**: MEDIUM | **Confidence**: High

**URL**: `http://192.168.1.49:3000/rest/admin`

**Description**: Content Security Policy (CSP) is an added layer of security that helps to detect and mitigate certain types of attacks, including Cross Site Scripting (XSS) and data injection attacks. These attacks are used for everything from data theft to site defacement or distribution of malware. CSP provides a set of standard HTTP headers that allow website owners to declare approved sources of content that browsers should be allowed to load on that page — covered types are JavaScript, CSS, HTML frames, fonts, images and embeddable objects such as Java applets, ActiveX, audio and video files.

**Solution**: Ensure that your web server, application server, load balancer, etc. is configured to set the Content-Security-Policy header.

---

### 145. Application Error Disclosure

**Risk**: LOW | **Confidence**: Medium

**URL**: `http://192.168.1.49:3000/rest/chatbot`

**Evidence**: `HTTP/1.1 500 Internal Server Error`

**Description**: This page contains an error/warning message that may disclose sensitive information like the location of the file that produced the unhandled exception. This information can be used to launch further attacks against the web application. The alert could be a false positive if the error message is found inside a documentation page.

**Solution**: Review the source code of this page. Implement custom error pages. Consider implementing a mechanism to provide a unique error reference/identifier to the client (browser) while logging the details on the server side and not exposing them to the user.

---

### 172. Cross-Domain Misconfiguration

**Risk**: MEDIUM | **Confidence**: Medium

**URL**: `http://192.168.1.49:3000/juice-shop/build/routes/verify.js:135:5`

**Evidence**: `Access-Control-Allow-Origin: *`

**Description**: Web browser data loading may be possible, due to a Cross Origin Resource Sharing (CORS) misconfiguration on the web server.

**Solution**: Ensure that sensitive data is not available in an unauthenticated manner (using IP address white-listing, for instance).
Configure the "Access-Control-Allow-Origin" HTTP header to a more restrictive set of domains, or remove all CORS headers entirely, to allow the web browser to enforce the Same Origin Policy (SOP) in a more restrictive manner.

---

### 173. Cross-Domain JavaScript Source File Inclusion

**Risk**: LOW | **Confidence**: Medium

**URL**: `http://192.168.1.49:3000/juice-shop/node_modules/express/lib/router/index.js:346:12`

**Evidence**: `<script src="//cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/jquery/2.2.4/jquery.min.js"></script>`

**Description**: The page includes one or more script files from a third-party domain.

**Solution**: Ensure JavaScript source files are loaded from only trusted sources, and the sources can't be controlled by end users of the application.

This information can be used to launch further attacks against the web application. The alert could be a false positive if the error message is found inside a documentation page.

### 216. Content Security Policy (CSP) Header Not Set

**URL**: `http://192.168.1.49:3000/juice-shop/build/lib/insecurity.js:111:34`

**Description**: Content Security Policy (CSP) is an added layer of security that helps to detect and mitigate certain types of attacks, including Cross Site Scripting (XSS) and data injection attacks. These attacks are used for everything from data theft to site defacement or distribution of malware. CSP provides a set of standard HTTP headers that allow website owners to declare approved sources of content that browsers should be allowed to load on that page — covered types are JavaScript, CSS, HTML frames, fonts, images and embeddable objects such as Java applets, ActiveX, audio and video files.

**Solution**: Ensure that your web server, application server, load balancer, etc. is configured to set the Content-Security-Policy header.

---

### 217. Content Security Policy (CSP) Header Not Set

### 218. Cross-Domain Misconfiguration

**Risk**: MEDIUM | **Confidence**: Medium

**URL**: `http://192.168.1.49:3000/juice-shop/build/lib/insecurity.js:111:34`

**Evidence**: `Access-Control-Allow-Origin: *`

**Description**: Web browser data loading may be possible, due to a Cross Origin Resource Sharing (CORS) misconfiguration on the web server.

**Solution**: Ensure that sensitive data is not available in an unauthenticated manner (using IP address white-listing, for instance).
Configure the "Access-Control-Allow-Origin" HTTP header to a more restrictive set of domains, or remove all CORS headers entirely, to allow the web browser to enforce the Same Origin Policy (SOP) in a more restrictive manner.

---

### 234. Application Error Disclosure

**Risk**: LOW | **Confidence**: Medium

**URL**: `http://192.168.1.49:3000/rest/order-history/:id`

**Evidence**: `HTTP/1.1 500 Internal Server Error`

**Description**: This page contains an error/warning message that may disclose sensitive information like the location of the file that produced the unhandled exception. This information can be used to launch further attacks against the web application. The alert could be a false positive if the error message is found inside a documentation page.

**Solution**: Review the source code of this page. Implement custom error pages. Consider implementing a mechanism to provide a unique error reference/identifier to the client (browser) while logging the details on the server side and not exposing them to the user.

**Description**: This page contains an error/warning message that may disclose sensitive information like the location of the file that produced the unhandled exception. This information can be used to launch further attacks against the web application. The alert could be a false positive if the error message is found inside a documentation page.

**Solution**: Review the source code of this page. Implement custom error pages. Consider implementing a mechanism to provide a unique error reference/identifier to the client (browser) while logging the details on the server side and not exposing them to the user.

---

### 261. Cross-Domain Misconfiguration

**Risk**: MEDIUM | **Confidence**: Medium

**URL**: `http://192.168.1.49:3000/vendor.js`

**Evidence**: `Access-Control-Allow-Origin: *`

**Description**: Web browser data loading may be possible, due to a Cross Origin Resource Sharing (CORS) misconfiguration on the web server.

**Solution**: Ensure that sensitive data is not available in an unauthenticated manner (using IP address white-listing, for instance).
Configure the "Access-Control-Allow-Origin" HTTP header to a more restrictive set of domains, or remove all CORS headers entirely, to allow the web browser to enforce the Same Origin Policy (SOP) in a more restrictive manner.

---

### 262. Content Security Policy (CSP) Header Not Set

**Risk**: MEDIUM | **Confidence**: High

**URL**: `http://192.168.1.49:3000/rest/track-order`

**Description**: Content Security Policy (CSP) is an added layer of security that helps to detect and mitigate certain types of attacks, including Cross Site Scripting (XSS) and data injection attacks. These attacks are used for everything from data theft to site defacement or distribution of malware. CSP provides a set of standard HTTP headers that allow website owners to declare approved sources of content that browsers should be allowed to load on that page — covered types are JavaScript, CSS, HTML frames, fonts, images and embeddable objects such as Java applets, ActiveX, audio and video files.

**Solution**: Ensure that your web server, application server, load balancer, etc. is configured to set the Content-Security-Policy header.

---

### 306. Content Security Policy (CSP) Header Not Set

**Risk**: MEDIUM | **Confidence**: High

**URL**: `http://192.168.1.49:3000/juice-shop/build/routes/vendor.js`

**Description**: Content Security Policy (CSP) is an added layer of security that helps to detect and mitigate certain types of attacks, including Cross Site Scripting (XSS) and data injection attacks. These attacks are used for everything from data theft to site defacement or distribution of malware. CSP provides a set of standard HTTP headers that allow website owners to declare approved sources of content that browsers should be allowed to load on that page — covered types are JavaScript, CSS, HTML frames, fonts, images and embeddable objects such as Java applets, ActiveX, audio and video files.

**Solution**: Ensure that your web server, application server, load balancer, etc. is configured to set the Content-Security-Policy header.

---

### 310. Cross-Domain Misconfiguration

**Risk**: MEDIUM | **Confidence**: Medium

**URL**: `http://192.168.1.49:3000/juice-shop/build/routes/vendor.js`

**Evidence**: `Access-Control-Allow-Origin: *`

**Description**: Web browser data loading may be possible, due to a Cross Origin Resource Sharing (CORS) misconfiguration on the web server.

**Solution**: Ensure that sensitive data is not available in an unauthenticated manner (using IP address white-listing, for instance).
Configure the "Access-Control-Allow-Origin" HTTP header to a more restrictive set of domains, or remove all CORS headers entirely, to allow the web browser to enforce the Same Origin Policy (SOP) in a more restrictive manner.

---

**Risk**: MEDIUM | **Confidence**: Medium

**URL**: `http://192.168.1.49:3000/juice-shop/node_modules/express/lib/router/polyfills.js`

**Evidence**: `Access-Control-Allow-Origin: *`

**Description**: Web browser data loading may be possible, due to a Cross Origin Resource Sharing (CORS) misconfiguration on the web server.

**Solution**: Ensure that sensitive data is not available in an unauthenticated manner (using IP address white-listing, for instance).
Configure the "Access-Control-Allow-Origin" HTTP header to a more restrictive set of domains, or remove all CORS headers entirely, to allow the web browser to enforce the Same Origin Policy (SOP) in a more restrictive manner.

---

### 351. Content Security Policy (CSP) Header Not Set

**Risk**: MEDIUM | **Confidence**: High

**URL**: `http://192.168.1.49:3000/juice-shop/node_modules/express/lib/router/vendor.js`

**Description**: Content Security Policy (CSP) is an added layer of security that helps to detect and mitigate certain types of attacks, including Cross Site Scripting (XSS) and data injection attacks. These attacks are used for everything from data theft to site defacement or distribution of malware. CSP provides a set of standard HTTP headers that allow website owners to declare approved sources of content that browsers should be allowed to load on that page — covered types are JavaScript, CSS, HTML frames, fonts, images and embeddable objects such as Java applets, ActiveX, audio and video files.

**Solution**: Ensure that your web server, application server, load balancer, etc. is configured to set the Content-Security-Policy header.

---

**URL**: `http://192.168.1.49:3000/juice-shop/build/lib/polyfills.js`

**Evidence**: `Access-Control-Allow-Origin: *`

**Description**: Web browser data loading may be possible, due to a Cross Origin Resource Sharing (CORS) misconfiguration on the web server.

**Solution**: Ensure that sensitive data is not available in an unauthenticated manner (using IP address white-listing, for instance).
Configure the "Access-Control-Allow-Origin" HTTP header to a more restrictive set of domains, or remove all CORS headers entirely, to allow the web browser to enforce the Same Origin Policy (SOP) in a more restrictive manner.

---

### 396. Modern Web Application

**Risk**: INFORMATIONAL | **Confidence**: Medium

**URL**: `http://192.168.1.49:3000/juice-shop/build/lib/styles.css`

**Evidence**: `<script src="//cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/cookieconsent2/3.1.0/cookieconsent.min.js"></script>`

**Description**: The application appears to be a modern web application. If you need to explore it automatically then the Ajax Spider may well be more effective than the standard one.

**Solution**: This is an informational alert and so no changes are required.

---

### 397. Content Security Policy (CSP) Header Not Set

**Risk**: MEDIUM | **Confidence**: High

**URL**: `http://192.168.1.49:3000/juice-shop/build/lib/assets/public/favicon_js.ico`

**Description**: Content Security Policy (CSP) is an added layer of security that helps to detect and mitigate certain types of attacks, including Cross Site Scripting (XSS) and data injection attacks. These attacks are used for everything from data theft to site defacement or distribution of malware. CSP provides a set of standard HTTP headers that allow website owners to declare approved sources of content that browsers should be allowed to load on that page — covered types are JavaScript, CSS, HTML frames, fonts, images and embeddable objects such as Java applets, ActiveX, audio and video files.

**Solution**: Ensure that your web server, application server, load balancer, etc. is configured to set the Content-Security-Policy header.

---

**Evidence**: `<script src="//cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/cookieconsent2/3.1.0/cookieconsent.min.js"></script>`

**Description**: The page includes one or more script files from a third-party domain.

**Solution**: Ensure JavaScript source files are loaded from only trusted sources, and the sources can't be controlled by end users of the application.

**Description**: Content Security Policy (CSP) is an added layer of security that helps to detect and mitigate certain types of attacks, including Cross Site Scripting (XSS) and data injection attacks. These attacks are used for everything from data theft to site defacement or distribution of malware. CSP provides a set of standard HTTP headers that allow website owners to declare approved sources of content that browsers should be allowed to load on that page — covered types are JavaScript, CSS, HTML frames, fonts, images and embeddable objects such as Java applets, ActiveX, audio and video files.

**Solution**: Ensure that your web server, application server, load balancer, etc. is configured to set the Content-Security-Policy header.

---

### 441. Cross-Domain Misconfiguration

**Risk**: MEDIUM | **Confidence**: Medium

**URL**: `http://192.168.1.49:3000/juice-shop/build/lib/main.js`

**Evidence**: `Access-Control-Allow-Origin: *`

**Description**: Web browser data loading may be possible, due to a Cross Origin Resource Sharing (CORS) misconfiguration on the web server.

**Solution**: Ensure that sensitive data is not available in an unauthenticated manner (using IP address white-listing, for instance).
Configure the "Access-Control-Allow-Origin" HTTP header to a more restrictive set of domains, or remove all CORS headers entirely, to allow the web browser to enforce the Same Origin Policy (SOP) in a more restrictive manner.

---

### 442. Cross-Domain JavaScript Source File Inclusion

**Risk**: LOW | **Confidence**: Medium

**URL**: `http://192.168.1.49:3000/juice-shop/build/lib/main.js`

**Evidence**: `<script src="//cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/cookieconsent2/3.1.0/cookieconsent.min.js"></script>`

**Description**: The page includes one or more script files from a third-party domain.

**Solution**: Ensure JavaScript source files are loaded from only trusted sources, and the sources can't be controlled by end users of the application.

---

**Description**: The application appears to be a modern web application. If you need to explore it automatically then the Ajax Spider may well be more effective than the standard one.

**Solution**: This is an informational alert and so no changes are required.

---

### 487. Cross-Domain Misconfiguration

**Risk**: MEDIUM | **Confidence**: Medium

**URL**: `http://192.168.1.49:3000/juice-shop/build/routes/assets/public/styles.css`

**Evidence**: `Access-Control-Allow-Origin: *`

**Description**: Web browser data loading may be possible, due to a Cross Origin Resource Sharing (CORS) misconfiguration on the web server.

**Solution**: Ensure that sensitive data is not available in an unauthenticated manner (using IP address white-listing, for instance).
Configure the "Access-Control-Allow-Origin" HTTP header to a more restrictive set of domains, or remove all CORS headers entirely, to allow the web browser to enforce the Same Origin Policy (SOP) in a more restrictive manner.

---

### 489. Content Security Policy (CSP) Header Not Set

**Risk**: MEDIUM | **Confidence**: High

**URL**: `http://192.168.1.49:3000/juice-shop/node_modules/morgan/assets/public/runtime.js`

**Description**: Content Security Policy (CSP) is an added layer of security that helps to detect and mitigate certain types of attacks, including Cross Site Scripting (XSS) and data injection attacks. These attacks are used for everything from data theft to site defacement or distribution of malware. CSP provides a set of standard HTTP headers that allow website owners to declare approved sources of content that browsers should be allowed to load on that page — covered types are JavaScript, CSS, HTML frames, fonts, images and embeddable objects such as Java applets, ActiveX, audio and video files.

**Solution**: Ensure that your web server, application server, load balancer, etc. is configured to set the Content-Security-Policy header.

---

**URL**: `http://192.168.1.49:3000/juice-shop/node_modules/graceful-fs/assets/public/runtime.js`

**Evidence**: `<script src="//cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/cookieconsent2/3.1.0/cookieconsent.min.js"></script>`

**Description**: The application appears to be a modern web application. If you need to explore it automatically then the Ajax Spider may well be more effective than the standard one.

**Solution**: This is an informational alert and so no changes are required.

---

### 531. Content Security Policy (CSP) Header Not Set

**Risk**: MEDIUM | **Confidence**: High

**URL**: `http://192.168.1.49:3000/juice-shop/node_modules/graceful-fs/assets/public/styles.css`

**Description**: Content Security Policy (CSP) is an added layer of security that helps to detect and mitigate certain types of attacks, including Cross Site Scripting (XSS) and data injection attacks. These attacks are used for everything from data theft to site defacement or distribution of malware. CSP provides a set of standard HTTP headers that allow website owners to declare approved sources of content that browsers should be allowed to load on that page — covered types are JavaScript, CSS, HTML frames, fonts, images and embeddable objects such as Java applets, ActiveX, audio and video files.

**Solution**: Ensure that your web server, application server, load balancer, etc. is configured to set the Content-Security-Policy header.

---

### 532. Cross-Domain Misconfiguration

**Risk**: MEDIUM | **Confidence**: Medium

**URL**: `http://192.168.1.49:3000/juice-shop/node_modules/graceful-fs/assets/public/styles.css`

**Evidence**: `Access-Control-Allow-Origin: *`

**Description**: Web browser data loading may be possible, due to a Cross Origin Resource Sharing (CORS) misconfiguration on the web server.

**Solution**: Ensure that sensitive data is not available in an unauthenticated manner (using IP address white-listing, for instance).
Configure the "Access-Control-Allow-Origin" HTTP header to a more restrictive set of domains, or remove all CORS headers entirely, to allow the web browser to enforce the Same Origin Policy (SOP) in a more restrictive manner.

---

### 533. Cross-Domain JavaScript Source File Inclusion

**Risk**: LOW | **Confidence**: Medium

**URL**: `http://192.168.1.49:3000/juice-shop/node_modules/graceful-fs/assets/public/styles.css`

**Evidence**: `<script src="//cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/cookieconsent2/3.1.0/cookieconsent.min.js"></script>`

**Description**: The page includes one or more script files from a third-party domain.

**Solution**: Ensure JavaScript source files are loaded from only trusted sources, and the sources can't be controlled by end users of the application.

---

**Solution**: Ensure JavaScript source files are loaded from only trusted sources, and the sources can't be controlled by end users of the application.

---

### 576. Content Security Policy (CSP) Header Not Set

**Risk**: MEDIUM | **Confidence**: High

**URL**: `http://192.168.1.49:3000/juice-shop/build/lib/assets/public/main.js`

**Description**: Content Security Policy (CSP) is an added layer of security that helps to detect and mitigate certain types of attacks, including Cross Site Scripting (XSS) and data injection attacks. These attacks are used for everything from data theft to site defacement or distribution of malware. CSP provides a set of standard HTTP headers that allow website owners to declare approved sources of content that browsers should be allowed to load on that page — covered types are JavaScript, CSS, HTML frames, fonts, images and embeddable objects such as Java applets, ActiveX, audio and video files.

**Solution**: Ensure that your web server, application server, load balancer, etc. is configured to set the Content-Security-Policy header.

---

### 577. Cross-Domain Misconfiguration

**Risk**: MEDIUM | **Confidence**: Medium

**URL**: `http://192.168.1.49:3000/juice-shop/build/lib/assets/public/main.js`

**Evidence**: `Access-Control-Allow-Origin: *`

**Description**: Web browser data loading may be possible, due to a Cross Origin Resource Sharing (CORS) misconfiguration on the web server.

**Solution**: Ensure that sensitive data is not available in an unauthenticated manner (using IP address white-listing, for instance).
Configure the "Access-Control-Allow-Origin" HTTP header to a more restrictive set of domains, or remove all CORS headers entirely, to allow the web browser to enforce the Same Origin Policy (SOP) in a more restrictive manner.

---

**URL**: `http://192.168.1.49:3000/juice-shop/build/routes/assets/public/assets/public/runtime.js`

**Description**: Content Security Policy (CSP) is an added layer of security that helps to detect and mitigate certain types of attacks, including Cross Site Scripting (XSS) and data injection attacks. These attacks are used for everything from data theft to site defacement or distribution of malware. CSP provides a set of standard HTTP headers that allow website owners to declare approved sources of content that browsers should be allowed to load on that page — covered types are JavaScript, CSS, HTML frames, fonts, images and embeddable objects such as Java applets, ActiveX, audio and video files.

**Solution**: Ensure that your web server, application server, load balancer, etc. is configured to set the Content-Security-Policy header.

---

### 619. Cross-Domain Misconfiguration

**Risk**: MEDIUM | **Confidence**: Medium

**URL**: `http://192.168.1.49:3000/juice-shop/build/routes/assets/public/assets/public/runtime.js`

**Evidence**: `Access-Control-Allow-Origin: *`

**Description**: Web browser data loading may be possible, due to a Cross Origin Resource Sharing (CORS) misconfiguration on the web server.

**Solution**: Ensure that sensitive data is not available in an unauthenticated manner (using IP address white-listing, for instance).
Configure the "Access-Control-Allow-Origin" HTTP header to a more restrictive set of domains, or remove all CORS headers entirely, to allow the web browser to enforce the Same Origin Policy (SOP) in a more restrictive manner.

---

### 620. Cross-Domain JavaScript Source File Inclusion

**Risk**: LOW | **Confidence**: Medium

**URL**: `http://192.168.1.49:3000/juice-shop/build/routes/assets/public/assets/public/runtime.js`

**Evidence**: `<script src="//cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/cookieconsent2/3.1.0/cookieconsent.min.js"></script>`

**Description**: The page includes one or more script files from a third-party domain.

**Solution**: Ensure JavaScript source files are loaded from only trusted sources, and the sources can't be controlled by end users of the application.

---

**Evidence**: `<script src="//cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/jquery/2.2.4/jquery.min.js"></script>`

**Description**: The page includes one or more script files from a third-party domain.

**Solution**: Ensure JavaScript source files are loaded from only trusted sources, and the sources can't be controlled by end users of the application.

### 663. Content Security Policy (CSP) Header Not Set

**Risk**: MEDIUM | **Confidence**: High

**URL**: `http://192.168.1.49:3000/juice-shop/node_modules/graceful-fs/assets/public/assets/public/styles.css`

**Description**: Content Security Policy (CSP) is an added layer of security that helps to detect and mitigate certain types of attacks, including Cross Site Scripting (XSS) and data injection attacks. These attacks are used for everything from data theft to site defacement or distribution of malware. CSP provides a set of standard HTTP headers that allow website owners to declare approved sources of content that browsers should be allowed to load on that page — covered types are JavaScript, CSS, HTML frames, fonts, images and embeddable objects such as Java applets, ActiveX, audio and video files.

**Solution**: Ensure that your web server, application server, load balancer, etc. is configured to set the Content-Security-Policy header.

---

### 664. Cross-Domain Misconfiguration

**Risk**: MEDIUM | **Confidence**: Medium

**URL**: `http://192.168.1.49:3000/juice-shop/node_modules/graceful-fs/assets/public/assets/public/styles.css`

**Evidence**: `Access-Control-Allow-Origin: *`

**Description**: Web browser data loading may be possible, due to a Cross Origin Resource Sharing (CORS) misconfiguration on the web server.

**Solution**: Ensure that sensitive data is not available in an unauthenticated manner (using IP address white-listing, for instance).
Configure the "Access-Control-Allow-Origin" HTTP header to a more restrictive set of domains, or remove all CORS headers entirely, to allow the web browser to enforce the Same Origin Policy (SOP) in a more restrictive manner.

---

CSP provides a set of standard HTTP headers that allow website owners to declare approved sources of content that browsers should be allowed to load on that page — covered types are JavaScript, CSS, HTML frames, fonts, images and embeddable objects such as Java applets, ActiveX, audio and video files.

**Solution**: Ensure that your web server, application server, load balancer, etc. is configured to set the Content-Security-Policy header.

---

### 705. Cross-Domain Misconfiguration

**Risk**: MEDIUM | **Confidence**: Medium

**URL**: `http://192.168.1.49:3000/juice-shop/build/lib/assets/public/assets/public/styles.css`

**Evidence**: `Access-Control-Allow-Origin: *`

**Description**: Web browser data loading may be possible, due to a Cross Origin Resource Sharing (CORS) misconfiguration on the web server.

**Solution**: Ensure that sensitive data is not available in an unauthenticated manner (using IP address white-listing, for instance).
Configure the "Access-Control-Allow-Origin" HTTP header to a more restrictive set of domains, or remove all CORS headers entirely, to allow the web browser to enforce the Same Origin Policy (SOP) in a more restrictive manner.

---

CSP provides a set of standard HTTP headers that allow website owners to declare approved sources of content that browsers should be allowed to load on that page — covered types are JavaScript, CSS, HTML frames, fonts, images and embeddable objects such as Java applets, ActiveX, audio and video files.

**Solution**: Ensure that your web server, application server, load balancer, etc. is configured to set the Content-Security-Policy header.

---

### 748. Content Security Policy (CSP) Header Not Set

**Risk**: MEDIUM | **Confidence**: High

**URL**: `http://192.168.1.49:3000/juice-shop/build/routes/assets/public/assets/public/assets/public/assets/public/favicon_js.ico`

**Description**: Content Security Policy (CSP) is an added layer of security that helps to detect and mitigate certain types of attacks, including Cross Site Scripting (XSS) and data injection attacks. These attacks are used for everything from data theft to site defacement or distribution of malware. CSP provides a set of standard HTTP headers that allow website owners to declare approved sources of content that browsers should be allowed to load on that page — covered types are JavaScript, CSS, HTML frames, fonts, images and embeddable objects such as Java applets, ActiveX, audio and video files.

**Solution**: Ensure that your web server, application server, load balancer, etc. is configured to set the Content-Security-Policy header.

---

### 749. Cross-Domain Misconfiguration

**Risk**: MEDIUM | **Confidence**: Medium

**URL**: `http://192.168.1.49:3000/juice-shop/node_modules/express/lib/router/assets/public/assets/public/assets/public/vendor.js`

**Evidence**: `Access-Control-Allow-Origin: *`

**Description**: Web browser data loading may be possible, due to a Cross Origin Resource Sharing (CORS) misconfiguration on the web server.

**Solution**: Ensure that sensitive data is not available in an unauthenticated manner (using IP address white-listing, for instance).
Configure the "Access-Control-Allow-Origin" HTTP header to a more restrictive set of domains, or remove all CORS headers entirely, to allow the web browser to enforce the Same Origin Policy (SOP) in a more restrictive manner.

---

**Risk**: MEDIUM | **Confidence**: High

**URL**: `http://192.168.1.49:3000/juice-shop/node_modules/morgan/assets/public/assets/public/assets/public/vendor.js`

**Description**: Content Security Policy (CSP) is an added layer of security that helps to detect and mitigate certain types of attacks, including Cross Site Scripting (XSS) and data injection attacks. These attacks are used for everything from data theft to site defacement or distribution of malware. CSP provides a set of standard HTTP headers that allow website owners to declare approved sources of content that browsers should be allowed to load on that page — covered types are JavaScript, CSS, HTML frames, fonts, images and embeddable objects such as Java applets, ActiveX, audio and video files.

**Solution**: Ensure that your web server, application server, load balancer, etc. is configured to set the Content-Security-Policy header.

---

### 791. Cross-Domain Misconfiguration

**Risk**: MEDIUM | **Confidence**: Medium

**URL**: `http://192.168.1.49:3000/juice-shop/node_modules/morgan/assets/public/assets/public/assets/public/vendor.js`

**Evidence**: `Access-Control-Allow-Origin: *`

**Description**: Web browser data loading may be possible, due to a Cross Origin Resource Sharing (CORS) misconfiguration on the web server.

**Solution**: Ensure that sensitive data is not available in an unauthenticated manner (using IP address white-listing, for instance).
Configure the "Access-Control-Allow-Origin" HTTP header to a more restrictive set of domains, or remove all CORS headers entirely, to allow the web browser to enforce the Same Origin Policy (SOP) in a more restrictive manner.

---

### 792. Cross-Domain JavaScript Source File Inclusion

**Risk**: LOW | **Confidence**: Medium

**URL**: `http://192.168.1.49:3000/juice-shop/node_modules/morgan/assets/public/assets/public/assets/public/vendor.js`

**Evidence**: `<script src="//cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/cookieconsent2/3.1.0/cookieconsent.min.js"></script>`

**Description**: The page includes one or more script files from a third-party domain.

**Solution**: Ensure JavaScript source files are loaded from only trusted sources, and the sources can't be controlled by end users of the application.

---

**Evidence**: `<script src="//cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/cookieconsent2/3.1.0/cookieconsent.min.js"></script>`

**Description**: The application appears to be a modern web application. If you need to explore it automatically then the Ajax Spider may well be more effective than the standard one.

### 833. Cross-Domain JavaScript Source File Inclusion

**Risk**: LOW | **Confidence**: Medium

**URL**: `http://192.168.1.49:3000/juice-shop/build/routes/assets/public/assets/public/assets/public/main.js`

**Evidence**: `<script src="//cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/cookieconsent2/3.1.0/cookieconsent.min.js"></script>`

**Description**: The page includes one or more script files from a third-party domain.

**Solution**: Ensure JavaScript source files are loaded from only trusted sources, and the sources can't be controlled by end users of the application.

---

### 834. Content Security Policy (CSP) Header Not Set

**Risk**: MEDIUM | **Confidence**: High

**URL**: `http://192.168.1.49:3000/juice-shop/node_modules/graceful-fs/assets/public/assets/public/assets/public/main.js`

**Description**: Content Security Policy (CSP) is an added layer of security that helps to detect and mitigate certain types of attacks, including Cross Site Scripting (XSS) and data injection attacks. These attacks are used for everything from data theft to site defacement or distribution of malware. CSP provides a set of standard HTTP headers that allow website owners to declare approved sources of content that browsers should be allowed to load on that page — covered types are JavaScript, CSS, HTML frames, fonts, images and embeddable objects such as Java applets, ActiveX, audio and video files.

**Solution**: Ensure that your web server, application server, load balancer, etc. is configured to set the Content-Security-Policy header.

---

### 835. Cross-Domain Misconfiguration

**Risk**: MEDIUM | **Confidence**: Medium

**URL**: `http://192.168.1.49:3000/juice-shop/node_modules/graceful-fs/assets/public/assets/public/assets/public/vendor.js`

**Evidence**: `Access-Control-Allow-Origin: *`

**Description**: Web browser data loading may be possible, due to a Cross Origin Resource Sharing (CORS) misconfiguration on the web server.

**Solution**: Ensure that sensitive data is not available in an unauthenticated manner (using IP address white-listing, for instance).
Configure the "Access-Control-Allow-Origin" HTTP header to a more restrictive set of domains, or remove all CORS headers entirely, to allow the web browser to enforce the Same Origin Policy (SOP) in a more restrictive manner.

---

**Evidence**: `<script src="//cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/cookieconsent2/3.1.0/cookieconsent.min.js"></script>`

**Description**: The application appears to be a modern web application. If you need to explore it automatically then the Ajax Spider may well be more effective than the standard one.

**Solution**: This is an informational alert and so no changes are required.

---

### 876. Cross-Domain Misconfiguration

**Risk**: MEDIUM | **Confidence**: Medium

**URL**: `http://192.168.1.49:3000/juice-shop/build/lib/assets/public/assets/public/assets/public/main.js`

**Evidence**: `Access-Control-Allow-Origin: *`

**Description**: Web browser data loading may be possible, due to a Cross Origin Resource Sharing (CORS) misconfiguration on the web server.

**Solution**: Ensure that sensitive data is not available in an unauthenticated manner (using IP address white-listing, for instance).
Configure the "Access-Control-Allow-Origin" HTTP header to a more restrictive set of domains, or remove all CORS headers entirely, to allow the web browser to enforce the Same Origin Policy (SOP) in a more restrictive manner.

---

### 890. Content Security Policy (CSP) Header Not Set

**Risk**: MEDIUM | **Confidence**: High

**URL**: `http://192.168.1.49:3000/ftp/coupons_2013.md.bak`

**Description**: Content Security Policy (CSP) is an added layer of security that helps to detect and mitigate certain types of attacks, including Cross Site Scripting (XSS) and data injection attacks. These attacks are used for everything from data theft to site defacement or distribution of malware. CSP provides a set of standard HTTP headers that allow website owners to declare approved sources of content that browsers should be allowed to load on that page — covered types are JavaScript, CSS, HTML frames, fonts, images and embeddable objects such as Java applets, ActiveX, audio and video files.

**Solution**: Ensure that your web server, application server, load balancer, etc. is configured to set the Content-Security-Policy header.

---

**Solution**: Ensure that your web server, application server, load balancer, etc. is configured to set the Content-Security-Policy header.

---

**Risk**: LOW | **Confidence**: Medium

**URL**: `http://192.168.1.49:3000/juice-shop/node_modules/graceful-fs/polyfills.js:306:20`

**Evidence**: `<script src="//cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/cookieconsent2/3.1.0/cookieconsent.min.js"></script>`

**Description**: The page includes one or more script files from a third-party domain.

**Solution**: Ensure JavaScript source files are loaded from only trusted sources, and the sources can't be controlled by end users of the application.

### 921. Cross-Domain Misconfiguration

**Risk**: MEDIUM | **Confidence**: Medium

**URL**: `http://192.168.1.49:3000/juice-shop/build/routes/fileServer.js:16:13`

**Evidence**: `Access-Control-Allow-Origin: *`

**Description**: Web browser data loading may be possible, due to a Cross Origin Resource Sharing (CORS) misconfiguration on the web server.

**Solution**: Ensure that sensitive data is not available in an unauthenticated manner (using IP address white-listing, for instance).
Configure the "Access-Control-Allow-Origin" HTTP header to a more restrictive set of domains, or remove all CORS headers entirely, to allow the web browser to enforce the Same Origin Policy (SOP) in a more restrictive manner.

**URL**: `http://192.168.1.49:3000/juice-shop/node_modules/serve-index/vendor.js`

---

### 964. Content Security Policy (CSP) Header Not Set

**Risk**: MEDIUM | **Confidence**: High

**URL**: `http://192.168.1.49:3000/juice-shop/node_modules/serve-index/assets/public/main.js`

**Description**: Content Security Policy (CSP) is an added layer of security that helps to detect and mitigate certain types of attacks, including Cross Site Scripting (XSS) and data injection attacks. These attacks are used for everything from data theft to site defacement or distribution of malware. CSP provides a set of standard HTTP headers that allow website owners to declare approved sources of content that browsers should be allowed to load on that page — covered types are JavaScript, CSS, HTML frames, fonts, images and embeddable objects such as Java applets, ActiveX, audio and video files.

**Solution**: Ensure that your web server, application server, load balancer, etc. is configured to set the Content-Security-Policy header.

---

### 965. Cross-Domain Misconfiguration

**Risk**: MEDIUM | **Confidence**: Medium

**URL**: `http://192.168.1.49:3000/juice-shop/node_modules/serve-index/assets/public/main.js`

**Evidence**: `Access-Control-Allow-Origin: *`

**Description**: Web browser data loading may be possible, due to a Cross Origin Resource Sharing (CORS) misconfiguration on the web server.

**Solution**: Ensure that sensitive data is not available in an unauthenticated manner (using IP address white-listing, for instance).
Configure the "Access-Control-Allow-Origin" HTTP header to a more restrictive set of domains, or remove all CORS headers entirely, to allow the web browser to enforce the Same Origin Policy (SOP) in a more restrictive manner.

---
